        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Steps to reproduce the problem:



<b class="line"><!---->Steps to reproduce the problem:<!----></b>



<br>





1. git apply repo.diff



<span class="line"><!---->1. git apply repo.diff<!----></span>



<br>





2. start chromium on MacOS m1



<span class="line"><!---->2. start chromium on MacOS m1<!----></span>



<br>





3. try to close the browser and destroyed the profile raw pointer



<span class="line"><!---->3. try to close the browser and destroyed the profile raw pointer<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Problem Description:



<b class="line"><!---->Problem Description:<!----></b>



<br>





There is a raw pointer `profile` [1] in posttask,if `profile` destroyed before [2],the UAF will be trigger.



<span class="line"><!---->There is a raw pointer `profile` [1] in posttask,if `profile` destroyed before [2],the UAF will be trigger.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=262?q=chrome%2Fbrowser%2Fsignin%2Fprimary_account_policy_manager.cc



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=262?q=chrome%2Fbrowser%2Fsignin%2Fprimary_account_policy_manager.cc"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=262?q=chrome%2Fbrowser%2Fsignin%2Fprimary_account_policy_manager.cc<!----></a>



<br>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=58;drc=50c7ef071b60980abc3ee4ec76bd04db4fb437b0?q=chrome%2Fbrowser%2Fsignin%2Fprimary_account_policy_manager.cc"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=58;drc=50c7ef071b60980abc3ee4ec76bd04db4fb437b0?q=chrome%2Fbrowser%2Fsignin%2Fprimary_account_policy_manager.cc<!----></a>

I looked a bit at this crash, and here are my initial observations:



<span class="line"><!---->I looked a bit at this crash, and here are my initial observations:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I don't think the description of the bug in the original report is accurate: this does not seem to be caused by a unretained profile, or related to PrimaryAccountPolicyManager::ShowDeleteProfileDialog.



<span class="line"><!---->I don't think the description of the bug in the original report is accurate: this does not seem to be caused by a unretained profile, or related to PrimaryAccountPolicyManager::ShowDeleteProfileDialog.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The crash is instead in PrimaryAccountPolicyManager::DeleteProfileDialogManager::ShowDeleteProfileDialog.



<span class="line"><!---->The crash is instead in PrimaryAccountPolicyManager::DeleteProfileDialogManager::ShowDeleteProfileDialog.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





From the linked stack traces, I see 2 different UAFs:



<span class="line"><!---->From the linked stack traces, I see 2 different UAFs:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





- in "asan", the object is a PrimaryAccountPolicyManager instance. Given the context, it should be the delegate_ field, used in HandleUserConfirmedProfileDeletionAndDie(). It's not clear how this can happen as the delegate is intended to own this object, so it should no be destroyed before this.



<span class="line"><!---->- in "asan", the object is a PrimaryAccountPolicyManager instance. Given the context, it should be the delegate_ field, used in HandleUserConfirmedProfileDeletionAndDie(). It's not clear how this can happen as the delegate is intended to own this object, so it should no be destroyed before this.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





- in "asan-windows", the object is a Browser instance. Again it's not super clear how this can happen, as DeleteProfileDialogManager listens for Browser destruction and there is logic to handle this case.



<span class="line"><!---->- in "asan-windows", the object is a Browser instance. Again it's not super clear how this can happen, as DeleteProfileDialogManager listens for Browser destruction and there is logic to handle this case.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We need more investigation.



<span class="line"><!---->We need more investigation.<!----></span>

My guess is that the problem is:



<span class="line"><!---->My guess is that the problem is:<!----></span>



<br>





- chrome::ShowWarningMessageBox() is used [1]



<span class="line"><!---->- chrome::ShowWarningMessageBox() is used [1]<!----></span>



<br>





- the message box uses a nestable loop [2]



<span class="line"><!---->- the message box uses a nestable loop [2]<!----></span>



<br>





- while the message box is shown, Chrome continues running in the background (because of the nested run loop) and the objects are destroyed (e.g. the profile, the browser)



<span class="line"><!---->- while the message box is shown, Chrome continues running in the background (because of the nested run loop) and the objects are destroyed (e.g. the profile, the browser)<!----></span>



<br>





- when chrome::ShowWarningMessageBox() returns, everything was destroyed and who knows what can happen after that



<span class="line"><!---->- when chrome::ShowWarningMessageBox() returns, everything was destroyed and who knows what can happen after that<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





gab, I see you added the nestable loop there: what do you think about the above scenario? If this is the right explanation, what would be the right fix? Would it be enough to check if we're still alive after ShowWarningMessageBox() returns (e.g. by checking active_browser_ and the weak_factory_)?



<span class="line"><!---->gab, I see you added the nestable loop there: what do you think about the above scenario? If this is the right explanation, what would be the right fix? Would it be enough to check if we're still alive after ShowWarningMessageBox() returns (e.g. by checking active_browser_ and the weak_factory_)?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=126;drc=843911a994428b40537550f48b52d0d58cf08dd3"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=126;drc=843911a994428b40537550f48b52d0d58cf08dd3<!----></a>

Thanks—as security sheriff, I had been puzzling over this because I didn't understand how we could UaF due to the WeakPtr. What I was missing was the nested run loop.



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks—as security sheriff, I had been puzzling over this because I didn't understand how we could UaF due to the WeakPtr. What I was missing was the nested run loop.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It sounds like it's possible for `this` to be deleted in the run loop though; in that case, we need to hold a WeakPtr to `this` on the stack and check if it's still valid after showing the dialog. If we do add the WeakPtr, it would be helpful to clearly document how we end up in this situation.



<span class="line"><!---->It sounds like it's possible for `this` to be deleted in the run loop though; in that case, we need to hold a WeakPtr to `this` on the stack and check if it's still valid after showing the dialog. If we do add the WeakPtr, it would be helpful to clearly document how we end up in this situation.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I guess the warning dialog is only psuedo-modal, and nothing stops the browser from being closed from behind it? Though in that case, I would have expected it to be a much easier UaF race to win. Can someone confirm? How do we trigger this dialog normally?



<span class="line"><!---->I guess the warning dialog is only psuedo-modal, and nothing stops the browser from being closed from behind it? Though in that case, I would have expected it to be a much easier UaF race to win. Can someone confirm? How do we trigger this dialog normally?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





One thing that's unclear to me is if the original patch is "realistic": the browser side patch that's required changes the control flow, and it's possible that the changed conditionals affect control flow in ways that are impossible in actual Chrome. I /think/ that's not the case though: the patch just makes it easier to hit this UaF without having sync fully set up for an account.



<span class="line"><!---->One thing that's unclear to me is if the original patch is "realistic": the browser side patch that's required changes the control flow, and it's possible that the changed conditionals affect control flow in ways that are impossible in actual Chrome. I /think/ that's not the case though: the patch just makes it easier to hit this UaF without having sync fully set up for an account.<!----></span>

I tried reproing the bug on Mac and I could not get it to trigger.



<span class="line"><!---->I tried reproing the bug on Mac and I could not get it to trigger.<!----></span>



<br>





At this point I am not sure if there is a bug or not.



<span class="line"><!---->At this point I am not sure if there is a bug or not.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In my attempts, I saw that background tasks were indeed processed while the modal dialog is shown.



<span class="line"><!---->In my attempts, I saw that background tasks were indeed processed while the modal dialog is shown.<!----></span>



<br>





However, when trying to close the browser from a background task, I had this sequence of events:



<span class="line"><!---->However, when trying to close the browser from a background task, I had this sequence of events:<!----></span>



<br>





- show the dialog ShowWarningMessageBox



<span class="line"><!---->- show the dialog ShowWarningMessageBox<!----></span>



<br>





- close the browser from a background task



<span class="line"><!---->- close the browser from a background task<!----></span>



<br>





- OnBrowserNoLongerActive is called



<span class="line"><!---->- OnBrowserNoLongerActive is called<!----></span>



<br>





- Dialog is automatically dismissed, ShowWarningMessageBox returns. At this point the browser is still alive, so there is no UaF



<span class="line"><!---->- Dialog is automatically dismissed, ShowWarningMessageBox returns. At this point the browser is still alive, so there is no UaF<!----></span>



<br>





- OnBrowserRemoved is called and the browser is destroyed



<span class="line"><!---->- OnBrowserRemoved is called and the browser is destroyed<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This sequence of events looks normal.



<span class="line"><!---->This sequence of events looks normal.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This code could definitely be improved (at least by adding comments), as the behavior related to the nestable run loop is super complex and not obvious at all. However so far I could not find a bug.



<span class="line"><!---->This code could definitely be improved (at least by adding comments), as the behavior related to the nestable run loop is super complex and not obvious at all. However so far I could not find a bug.<!----></span>



<br>





We could possibly land the speculative fix (



<span class="line"><!---->We could possibly land the speculative fix (<!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3757856



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3757856"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3757856<!----></a>





)



<span class="line"><!---->)<!----></span>





 as it seems to fix the bug for the reporter, but I still don't understand the issue myself.



<span class="line"><!----> as it seems to fix the bug for the reporter, but I still don't understand the issue myself.<!----></span>

Thank you for your reply. For me, it is more convenient to reproduce this vulnerability on windows, although I have to apply a patch of the browser process, but I do not intend to create a situation that is impossible to trigger, or fake an asan log.



<span class="line"><!---->Thank you for your reply. For me, it is more convenient to reproduce this vulnerability on windows, although I have to apply a patch of the browser process, but I do not intend to create a situation that is impossible to trigger, or fake an asan log.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The call stack of this vulnerability is roughly as follows:



<span class="line"><!---->The call stack of this vulnerability is roughly as follows:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=126;drc=843911a994428b40537550f48b52d0d58cf08dd3"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/signin/primary_account_policy_manager.cc;l=126;drc=843911a994428b40537550f48b52d0d58cf08dd3<!----></a>

<br>





[2] 



<span class="line"><!---->[2] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=298;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=298;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=298;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a<!----></a>

[3] 



<span class="line"><!---->[3] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=107;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=107;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=107;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a<!----></a>

[4] 



<span class="line"><!---->[4] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=88;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=88;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/browser/ui/views/message_box_dialog.cc;l=88;drc=ff739842eaf3ee00c4af77861b63e984d2e75d7a<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





So if we execute `<script>window.close();</script>` in the run loop,everything was destroyed,then uaf will be triggered after [1] return.



<span class="line"><!---->So if we execute `&lt;script&gt;window.close();&lt;/script&gt;` in the run loop,everything was destroyed,then uaf will be triggered after [1] return.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I can trigger very stable on windows and mac environments compiled with asan chromium, just like the steps in my previous video.



<span class="line"><!---->I can trigger very stable on windows and mac environments compiled with asan chromium, just like the steps in my previous video.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





However, a sleep needs to be added in the mac environment. After my analysis, the added sleep may be a bit far-fetched, which is why I mentioned it at the beginning. I tried nearly 50 times and only succeeded twice.



<span class="line"><!---->However, a sleep needs to be added in the mac environment. After my analysis, the added sleep may be a bit far-fetched, which is why I mentioned it at the beginning. I tried nearly 50 times and only succeeded twice.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





But I still think this is a case that can be triggered, just follow the above call stack in sequence [1][2][3][4], and then execute `<script>window.close();</script>`.



<span class="line"><!---->But I still think this is a case that can be triggered, just follow the above call stack in sequence [1][2][3][4], and then execute `&lt;script&gt;window.close();&lt;/script&gt;`.<!----></span>

Are you sure the script is executed? `<script>window.close();</script>`



<span class="line"><!---->Are you sure the script is executed? `&lt;script&gt;window.close();&lt;/script&gt;`<!----></span>



<br>





For me on Mac it does not execute. I have a javascript error: "scripts can only close windows opened by them"



<span class="line"><!---->For me on Mac it does not execute. I have a javascript error: "scripts can only close windows opened by them"<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I can close the browser programatically in C++ with:



<span class="line"><!---->I can close the browser programatically in C++ with:<!----></span>



<br>





    base::ThreadTaskRunnerHandle::Get()->PostDelayedTask(



<span class="line"><!---->    base::ThreadTaskRunnerHandle::Get()-&gt;PostDelayedTask(<!----></span>



<br>





            FROM_HERE,



<span class="line"><!---->            FROM_HERE,<!----></span>



<br>





            base::BindOnce(&ui::BaseWindow::Close, base::Unretained(browser->window())),



<span class="line"><!---->            base::BindOnce(&amp;ui::BaseWindow::Close, base::Unretained(browser-&gt;window())),<!----></span>



<br>





            base::Seconds(1));



<span class="line"><!---->            base::Seconds(1));<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This works and indeed closes the browser while the dialog is shown, but it does not crash.



<span class="line"><!---->This works and indeed closes the browser while the dialog is shown, but it does not crash.<!----></span>

If you manually open a new tab page, that is, through input event, then it is not possible to close it by executing `window.close();` through javascript. JavaScript's window.close(); can only close pages created by JavaScript `window.open();`



<span class="line"><!---->If you manually open a new tab page, that is, through input event, then it is not possible to close it by executing `window.close();` through javascript. JavaScript's window.close(); can only close pages created by JavaScript `window.open();`<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In order to reproduce the vulnerabilities related to `window.close();` more conveniently, we will often directly write the link we want to access in the command line parameters of starting chrome, such as: `./out/asan- chromium/chrome.exe 



<span class="line"><!---->In order to reproduce the vulnerabilities related to `window.close();` more conveniently, we will often directly write the link we want to access in the command line parameters of starting chrome, such as: `./out/asan- chromium/chrome.exe <!----></span>





http://127.0.0.1:8000/index.html`



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://127.0.0.1:8000/index.html`"><!---->http://127.0.0.1:8000/index.html`<!----></a>





.



<span class="line"><!---->.<!----></span>





 The tab page created in this way is not a page manually created by input event, so it can execute `window.close();` of JavaScript.



<span class="line"><!----> The tab page created in this way is not a page manually created by input event, so it can execute `window.close();` of JavaScript.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





A more common situation is that we will open a first tab, create a second tab by `window.open();`, and then `setTimeout(()=>window.close(),8000);` to close the second tab to close it and trigger a similar vulnerability.



<span class="line"><!---->A more common situation is that we will open a first tab, create a second tab by `window.open();`, and then `setTimeout(()=&gt;window.close(),8000);` to close the second tab to close it and trigger a similar vulnerability.<!----></span>

I am very sorry that my previous description may not be in place, causing unnecessary trouble and confusion to you.Let me give a more detailed summary of the current situation.This might be a bit verbose, but I really wanted to share it with you.



<span class="line"><!---->I am very sorry that my previous description may not be in place, causing unnecessary trouble and confusion to you.Let me give a more detailed summary of the current situation.This might be a bit verbose, but I really wanted to share it with you.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This vulnerability is indeed discovered by me by accident. At first, I was just trying to test an posttask unretained profile UAF, but the UAF of the message loop was unintentionally triggered.Many thanks to droger for correcting my mistake in time.



<span class="line"><!---->This vulnerability is indeed discovered by me by accident. At first, I was just trying to test an posttask unretained profile UAF, but the UAF of the message loop was unintentionally triggered.Many thanks to droger for correcting my mistake in time.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





At the beginning I couldn't trigger it on linux at all, so I tried it on MacOS and Windows,and both succeeded.



<span class="line"><!---->At the beginning I couldn't trigger it on linux at all, so I tried it on MacOS and Windows,and both succeeded.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





**But I think Windows should be the most reasonable operating system to reproduce this vulnerability at present**



<span class="line"><!---->**But I think Windows should be the most reasonable operating system to reproduce this vulnerability at present**<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In the last week, I reproduced and learned some message loop UAF vulnerability I could find,take this bug as an example:



<span class="line"><!---->In the last week, I reproduced and learned some message loop UAF vulnerability I could find,take this bug as an example:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





- TabStrip drag and drop



<span class="line"><!---->- TabStrip drag and drop<!----></span>



<br>





https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1138911



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1138911"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1138911<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





It can be successfully reproduced on linux, but I can't reproduce it on MacOS.At this time, I began to suspect that the uaf related to the message loop run loop may be related to the operating system.



<span class="line"><!---->It can be successfully reproduced on linux, but I can't reproduce it on MacOS.At this time, I began to suspect that the uaf related to the message loop run loop may be related to the operating system.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





As it stands, I can still successfully(?) reproduce the bug on MacOS, but I need to patch a `sleep(8);` to give me an opportunity to close the page while the run_loop is executing.



<span class="line"><!---->As it stands, I can still successfully(?) reproduce the bug on MacOS, but I need to patch a `sleep(8);` to give me an opportunity to close the page while the run_loop is executing.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





But in the current situation, this `sleep(8);` of my patch may be an unreasonable scene. Just like other message loop UAF vulnerabilities, I initially thought that on MacOS, we only need to make the page execute `window.close();` when the run loop is executed. But the steps I reproduced in the video use the time window of `sleep(8);` to manually click the close button of the tab once, and it may be this tiny action that caused the strange exception.



<span class="line"><!---->But in the current situation, this `sleep(8);` of my patch may be an unreasonable scene. Just like other message loop UAF vulnerabilities, I initially thought that on MacOS, we only need to make the page execute `window.close();` when the run loop is executed. But the steps I reproduced in the video use the time window of `sleep(8);` to manually click the close button of the tab once, and it may be this tiny action that caused the strange exception.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The timing of this `sleep` may not be particularly reasonable, unless we can control some logic to delay chrome during the execution of the code.If I delete this `sleep(8);`, then I can't reproduce it successfully on MacOS, which may also be the case for you.



<span class="line"><!---->The timing of this `sleep` may not be particularly reasonable, unless we can control some logic to delay chrome during the execution of the code.If I delete this `sleep(8);`, then I can't reproduce it successfully on MacOS, which may also be the case for you.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





But on Windows, there is absolutely no need to patch any sleep or delayed callbacks to trigger the vulnerability.According to my previous theory, this vulnerability should be real, not a fake vulnerability, nor a scene that I maliciously faked.So I think we can modify the OS affected by the vulnerability to be Windows only.



<span class="line"><!---->But on Windows, there is absolutely no need to patch any sleep or delayed callbacks to trigger the vulnerability.According to my previous theory, this vulnerability should be real, not a fake vulnerability, nor a scene that I maliciously faked.So I think we can modify the OS affected by the vulnerability to be Windows only.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In the end, I think the fix for this bug is justified, almost the same as the fix for this bug.



<span class="line"><!---->In the end, I think the fix for this bug is justified, almost the same as the fix for this bug.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2481074



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2481074"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2481074<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





Please let me know if you need more info about it.



<span class="line"><!---->Please let me know if you need more info about it.<!----></span>
